## γ (id: 001049000000000)

γ
=

γ

noun nom

60\.50 · Number · First, Second, Third, Etc. \[Ordinals]

third third in a series involving either time, space, or set Occurring only in titles of NT writings: Ἰωάννου γ ‘Third Letter of John.’



## Γαββαθά (id: 001050000000000)

Γαββαθά
=======

Γαββαθά (G1042) — Γαββαθα

noun nom

93\.437 · Names of Persons and Places · Places

Gabbatha the Aramaic name for a paved area outside the residence of Pontius Pilate and the setting for the public trial of Jesus; see [7\.71](#7.71)

[JHN 19:13](https://ref.ly/Luke19:13)

* **Associated Passages:** John 19:13

## γαζοφυλάκιον (id: 001058000000000)

γαζοφυλάκιον
============

γαζοφυλάκιον (G1049)

noun

7\.33 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

treasury, Temple treasury a room in the Temple used as a treasury It is possible that in [JHN 8:20](https://ref.ly/Luke8:20) γαζοφυλάκιον designates the offering boxes rather than the treasury itself (see γαζοφυλάκιον\[b], [6\.141](#6.141)). If one interprets γαζοφυλάκιον in [JHN 8:20](https://ref.ly/Luke8:20) as the offering boxes, then one may translate ‘he spoke these words near where the offering boxes were.’

[JHN 8:20](https://ref.ly/Luke8:20)

6\.141 · Artifacts · Containers

offering box a large box in which offerings were placed The offering box in the Temple was also referred to as δῶρον\[b] ([6\.142](#6.142)).

[MRK 12:41](https://ref.ly/Matt12:41) · [MRK 12:41](https://ref.ly/Matt12:41) · [MRK 12:43](https://ref.ly/Matt12:43) · [LUK 21:1](https://ref.ly/Mark21:1) · [JHN 8:20](https://ref.ly/Luke8:20)

* **Associated Passages:** John 8:20; Mark 12:41; Mark 12:43; Luke 21:1

## γάλα (id: 001060000000000)

γάλα
====

γάλα (G1051)

noun

5\.19 · Foods and Condiments · Food

milk white fluid secreted by women and female mammals for nourishment of their young; also used as food for humans The term γάλα may refer to any type of milk, whether produced by humans or by certain domesticated animals, for example, cow, sheep, goat, camel.\|In a number of languages two distinct terms are used for milk, one identifying the human milk and another term specifying milk from animals. In the context of [1CO 3:2](https://ref.ly/Rom3:2) it is probably the latter reference which is important, though the passage is highly figurative and the emphasis is upon food for babies.1

[1CO 3:2](https://ref.ly/Rom3:2) · [1CO 9:7](https://ref.ly/Rom9:7) · [HEB 5:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:12) · [HEB 5:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:13) · [1PE 2:2](https://ref.ly/Jas2:2)

1 The meanings of ᾠόν ‘egg’ ([5\.18](#5.18)) and γάλα ‘milk’ ([5\.19](#5.19)) could be classified under Body Products in Domain 8, but in the NT contexts the focus is upon these products as food and not upon the physiological processes involved in producing such products.

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 3:2; 1 Corinthians 9:7; Hebrews 5:12; Hebrews 5:13; 1 Peter 2:2

## γαλήνη (id: 001064000000000)

γαλήνη
======

γαλήνη (G1055)

noun

14\.23 · Physical Events and States · Events Involving Liquids and Dry Masses

a calm (in contrast with a storm over water) a calm or unruffled surface of a body of water A calm after a storm may be referred to figuratively in some languages as ‘the water lay down’ or ‘the waves sank down again’ or ‘the water became like a table top.’

[MAT 8:26](https://ref.ly/Matt8:26) · [MRK 4:39](https://ref.ly/Matt4:39) · [LUK 8:24](https://ref.ly/Mark8:24)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 8:26; Mark 4:39; Luke 8:24

## γαμέω (id: 001070000000000)

γαμέω
=====

γαμέω (G1060)

ἄγαμος · γαμίζω · γαμίσκω · γάμος · ἐπιγαμβρεύω

34\.66 · Association · Marriage, Divorce

to marry, marriage to enter into a marriage relation, applicable either to a man or to a woman1

[MAT 5:32](https://ref.ly/Matt5:32) · [MAT 19:9](https://ref.ly/Matt19:9) · [MAT 19:10](https://ref.ly/Matt19:10) · [MAT 22:25](https://ref.ly/Matt22:25) · [MAT 22:30](https://ref.ly/Matt22:30) · [MAT 24:38](https://ref.ly/Matt24:38) · [MRK 6:17](https://ref.ly/Matt6:17) · [MRK 10:11](https://ref.ly/Matt10:11) · [MRK 10:12](https://ref.ly/Matt10:12) · [MRK 12:25](https://ref.ly/Matt12:25) · [LUK 14:20](https://ref.ly/Mark14:20) · [LUK 16:18](https://ref.ly/Mark16:18) · [LUK 16:18](https://ref.ly/Mark16:18) · [LUK 17:27](https://ref.ly/Mark17:27) · [LUK 20:34](https://ref.ly/Mark20:34) · [LUK 20:35](https://ref.ly/Mark20:35) · [1CO 7:9](https://ref.ly/Rom7:9) · [1CO 7:9](https://ref.ly/Rom7:9) · [1CO 7:10](https://ref.ly/Rom7:10) · [1CO 7:28](https://ref.ly/Rom7:28) · [1CO 7:28](https://ref.ly/Rom7:28) · [1CO 7:33](https://ref.ly/Rom7:33) · [1CO 7:34](https://ref.ly/Rom7:34) · [1CO 7:36](https://ref.ly/Rom7:36) · [1CO 7:39](https://ref.ly/Rom7:39) · [1TI 4:3](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:3) · [1TI 5:11](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:11) · [1TI 5:14](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:14)

1 γάμος\[a] differs in meaning from γαμέω and γαμίζω\[a] ([34\.66](#34.66)) in denoting the state of being married and not simply the act of entering into a marriage relation.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:32; Matthew 19:9; Matthew 19:10; Matthew 22:25; Matthew 22:30; Matthew 24:38; Mark 6:17; Mark 10:11; Mark 10:12; Mark 12:25; Luke 14:20; Luke 16:18; Luke 17:27; Luke 20:34; Luke 20:35; 1 Corinthians 7:9; 1 Corinthians 7:10; 1 Corinthians 7:28; 1 Corinthians 7:33; 1 Corinthians 7:34; 1 Corinthians 7:36; 1 Corinthians 7:39; 1 Timothy 4:3; 1 Timothy 5:11; 1 Timothy 5:14


## γαμίζω (id: 001071000000000)

γαμίζω
======

γαμίζω (G1061a) — γαμίσκω

γαμέω

34\.66 · Association · Marriage, Divorce

to marry, marriage to enter into a marriage relation, applicable either to a man or to a woman1 Some interpreters understand γαμίζω in [1CO 7:38](https://ref.ly/Rom7:38) to mean ‘to give in marriage’ (see [34\.72](#34.72)). See also the discussion at [13\.32](#13.32).

[1CO 7:38](https://ref.ly/Rom7:38) · [1CO 7:38](https://ref.ly/Rom7:38)

34\.72 · Association · Marriage, Divorce

to give in marriage to cause a person to become married

[MAT 22:30](https://ref.ly/Matt22:30) · [MAT 24:38](https://ref.ly/Matt24:38) · [MRK 12:25](https://ref.ly/Matt12:25) · [LUK 17:27](https://ref.ly/Mark17:27) · [LUK 20:34](https://ref.ly/Mark20:34) · [LUK 20:35](https://ref.ly/Mark20:35)

1 γάμος\[a] differs in meaning from γαμέω and γαμίζω\[a] ([34\.66](#34.66)) in denoting the state of being married and not simply the act of entering into a marriage relation.

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 7:38; Matthew 22:30; Matthew 24:38; Mark 12:25; Luke 17:27; Luke 20:34; Luke 20:35


## γάμος (id: 001072000000000)

γάμος
=====

γάμος (G1062)

noun · γαμέω

34\.67 · Association · Marriage, Divorce

marriage the state of being married1

[HEB 13:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:4)

34\.68 · Association · Marriage, Divorce

wedding the ceremony associated with becoming married

[MAT 22:2](https://ref.ly/Matt22:2) · [MAT 22:3](https://ref.ly/Matt22:3) · [MAT 22:4](https://ref.ly/Matt22:4) · [MAT 22:8](https://ref.ly/Matt22:8) · [MAT 22:9](https://ref.ly/Matt22:9) · [MAT 22:10](https://ref.ly/Matt22:10)2 · [MAT 22:11](https://ref.ly/Matt22:11) · [MAT 22:12](https://ref.ly/Matt22:12) · [MAT 25:10](https://ref.ly/Matt25:10) · [LUK 12:36](https://ref.ly/Mark12:36) · [LUK 14:8](https://ref.ly/Mark14:8) · [JHN 2:1](https://ref.ly/Luke2:1) · [JHN 2:2](https://ref.ly/Luke2:2) · [HEB 13:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:4) · [REV 19:7](https://ref.ly/Jude19:7) · [REV 19:9](https://ref.ly/Jude19:9)

7\.34 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

wedding hall a relatively large room, often serving as a place for a wedding In [MAT 22:10](https://ref.ly/Matt22:10) a number of manuscripts read νυμφών rather than γάμος.

[MAT 22:10](https://ref.ly/Matt22:10)2

1 γάμος\[a] differs in meaning from γαμέω and γαμίζω\[a] ([34\.66](#34.66)) in denoting the state of being married and not simply the act of entering into a marriage relation. 2 MAT 22:10 Though the meaning of νυμφών and γάμος\[c] in [MAT 22:10](https://ref.ly/Matt22:10) is basically the same, νυμφών may still carry semantic associations relating to the bride, while γάμος\[c] may have semantic associations which point more specifically to the celebration of a wedding.

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 13:4; Matthew 22:2; Matthew 22:3; Matthew 22:4; Matthew 22:8; Matthew 22:9; Matthew 22:10; Matthew 22:11; Matthew 22:12; Matthew 25:10; Luke 12:36; Luke 14:8; John 2:1; John 2:2; Revelation 19:7; Revelation 19:9

γάρ

cj

1:7](https://ref.ly/2John1:7)

91\.1 · Discourse Markers · Markers of Transition

and, then a marker of a new sentence, but often best left untranslated or reflected in the use of ‘and’ or the conjunctive adverb ‘then.’ It is possible that in [MAT 27:23](https://ref.ly/Matt27:23) the conjunction γάρ reflects Pilate’s attempt to reason with the crowd demanding Jesus’ crucifixion, but γάρ serves primarily to highlight the significance of the question rather than to provide a reason.

## γαστήρ (id: 001074000000000)

γαστήρ
======

γαστήρ (G1064)

noun

8\.68 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

belly, stomach, womb the inward parts of the body, either the digestive system (as in γαστέρες ἀργαί, literally ‘lazy bellies,’ but meaning ‘gluttons’ [TIT 1:12](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:12)) or the womb (in set phrases such as συλλαμβάνω ἐν γαστρί ‘to conceive’ [LUK 1:31](https://ref.ly/Mark1:31); ἐν γαστρὶ ἔχω ‘be pregnant’ [MAT 1:18](https://ref.ly/Matt1:18) and elsewhere) See also [23\.19](#23.19), [23\.49](#23.49), and [23\.50](#23.50).

[LUK 1:31](https://ref.ly/Mark1:31)

23\.19 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

glutton (a figurative extension of meaning of γαστήρ\[a] ‘belly,’ [8\.68](#8.68)) a person who habitually eats excessively A glutton is often spoken of idiomatically, for example, ‘a large belly’ or ‘a person who is only a stomach’ or ‘a professional eater.’

[TIT 1:12](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:12)

23\.50 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

**Collocation:** ἐν γαστρὶ ἔχω

pregnant, to be pregnant (an idiom, literally: to have in the womb) to be in a state of pregnancy This expression contrasts with the meaning of συλλαμβάνω\[b], [23\.49](#23.49), in that it seems to focus more upon the state of pregnancy rather than the event of conception.\|It is impossible to determine whether in [MAT 1:23](https://ref.ly/Matt1:23) (ἐν γαστρὶ ἕξει καὶ τέξεται υἱόν ‘she will be pregnant and bear a son’) the focus is upon the state of pregnancy or the fact of conception (see [23\.49](#23.49)).

[MAT 1:18](https://ref.ly/Matt1:18) · [MAT 1:23](https://ref.ly/Matt1:23) · [MAT 24:19](https://ref.ly/Matt24:19) · [MRK 13:17](https://ref.ly/Matt13:17) · [LUK 21:23](https://ref.ly/Mark21:23) · [1TH 5:3](https://ref.ly/Col5:3) · [REV 12:2](https://ref.ly/Jude12:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:31; Titus 1:12; Matthew 1:18; Matthew 1:23; Matthew 24:19; Mark 13:17; Luke 21:23; 1 Thessalonians 5:3; Revelation 12:2

then, indeed marker of relatively weak emphasis This word is frequently not translated but possibly reflected in the word order.

## γέεννα (id: 001078000000000)

γέεννα
======

γέεννα (G1067)

noun

1\.21 · Geographical Objects and Features · Regions Below the Surface of the Earth

Gehenna, hell a place of punishment for the dead The Greek term γέεννα is derived from a Hebrew phrase meaning ‘Valley of Hinnom,’ a ravine running along the south side of Jerusalem and a place where the rubbish from the city was constantly being burned. According to late Jewish popular belief, the last judgment was to take place in this valley, and hence the figurative extension of meaning from ‘Valley of Hinnom’ to ‘hell.’ In most languages γέεννα is rendered as ‘place of punishment’ or ‘place where the dead suffer’ or ‘place where the dead suffer because of their sins.’

[MAT 5:22](https://ref.ly/Matt5:22) · [MAT 5:29](https://ref.ly/Matt5:29) · [MAT 5:30](https://ref.ly/Matt5:30) · [MAT 10:28](https://ref.ly/Matt10:28) · [MAT 18:9](https://ref.ly/Matt18:9) · [MAT 23:15](https://ref.ly/Matt23:15) · [MAT 23:33](https://ref.ly/Matt23:33) · [MRK 9:43](https://ref.ly/Matt9:43) · [MRK 9:45](https://ref.ly/Matt9:45) · [MRK 9:47](https://ref.ly/Matt9:47) · [LUK 12:5](https://ref.ly/Mark12:5) · [JAS 3:6](https://ref.ly/Heb3:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:22; Matthew 5:29; Matthew 5:30; Matthew 10:28; Matthew 18:9; Matthew 23:15; Matthew 23:33; Mark 9:43; Mark 9:45; Mark 9:47; Luke 12:5; James 3:6

## γείτων (id: 001080000000000)

γείτων
======

γείτων (G1069)

noun

11\.89 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

neighbor, brother a person who lives close beside others and who thus by implication is a part of a so\-called in\-group, that is, the group with which an individual identifies both ethnically and culturally It may be that of the three terms γείτων, περίοικος\[b], the last is somewhat broader in meaning. At least πλησίον is used in [LUK 10:27](https://ref.ly/Mark10:27) in a somewhat extended sense of ‘fellow man,’ while ἀδελφός\[e] probably suggests a more intimate or close relationship.

[LUK 14:12](https://ref.ly/Mark14:12) · [LUK 15:6](https://ref.ly/Mark15:6) · [LUK 15:9](https://ref.ly/Mark15:9) · [JHN 9:8](https://ref.ly/Luke9:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 14:12; Luke 15:6; Luke 15:9; John 9:8


## γελάω (id: 001081000000000)

γελάω
=====

γελάω (G1070)

γέλως · καταγελάω

25\.135 · Attitudes and Emotions · Laugh, Cry, Groan

to laugh A number of languages distinguish clearly between various types of laughter: (1\) laughter directed against some person as a form of ridicule; (2\) laughter resulting from seeing some humorous event or as the result of listening to a humorous account; and (3\) laughter which reflects happiness and joy. In [LUK 6:21](https://ref.ly/Mark6:21) and [JAS 4:9](https://ref.ly/Heb4:9) it is this third type of laughter which is relevant to the contexts.

[LUK 6:21](https://ref.ly/Mark6:21) · [LUK 6:25](https://ref.ly/Mark6:25)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 6:21; Luke 6:25

## γενεά (id: 001085000000000)

γενεά
=====

γενεά (G1074)

noun · γίνομαι

11\.4 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · General

those of the same time, those of the same generation people living at the same time and belonging to the same reproductive age\-class The expression ‘the people of this generation’ may also be expressed as ‘the people living now’ or ‘the people of this time.’ Successive generations may be spoken of as ‘groups of people who live one after the other’ or ‘successions of parents and children.’

[MAT 11:16](https://ref.ly/Matt11:16) · [MAT 12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39) · [MAT 12:41](https://ref.ly/Matt12:41) · [MAT 12:42](https://ref.ly/Matt12:42) · [MAT 12:45](https://ref.ly/Matt12:45) · [MAT 16:4](https://ref.ly/Matt16:4) · [MAT 17:17](https://ref.ly/Matt17:17) · [MAT 23:36](https://ref.ly/Matt23:36) · [MAT 24:34](https://ref.ly/Matt24:34) · [MRK 8:12](https://ref.ly/Matt8:12) · [MRK 8:12](https://ref.ly/Matt8:12) · [MRK 8:38](https://ref.ly/Matt8:38) · [MRK 9:19](https://ref.ly/Matt9:19) · [MRK 13:30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:30) · [LUK 7:31](https://ref.ly/Mark7:31) · [LUK 9:41](https://ref.ly/Mark9:41) · [LUK 11:29](https://ref.ly/Mark11:29) · [LUK 11:29](https://ref.ly/Mark11:29) · [LUK 11:30](https://ref.ly/Mark11:30) · [LUK 11:31](https://ref.ly/Mark11:31) · [LUK 11:32](https://ref.ly/Mark11:32) · [LUK 11:50](https://ref.ly/Mark11:50) · [LUK 11:51](https://ref.ly/Mark11:51) · [LUK 17:25](https://ref.ly/Mark17:25) · [LUK 21:32](https://ref.ly/Mark21:32) · [ACT 13:36](https://ref.ly/John13:36) · [PHP 2:15](https://ref.ly/Eph2:15) · [HEB 3:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:10)

10\.4 · Kinship Terms · Groups and Members of Groups of Persons Regarded as Related by Blood but without Special Reference to Successive Generations

people of the same kind an ethnic group exhibiting cultural similarities Compare γενεά\[a] those of the same time ([11\.4](#11.4)).

[MAT 23:36](https://ref.ly/Matt23:36) · [MAT 24:34](https://ref.ly/Matt24:34) · [MRK 13:30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:30) · [LUK 16:8](https://ref.ly/Mark16:8) · [LUK 21:32](https://ref.ly/Mark21:32) · [ACT 2:40](https://ref.ly/John2:40) · [HEB 3:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:10)

10\.28 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations Involving Successive Generations

posterity, descendants, offspring successive following generations of those who are biologically related to a reference person In the case of γενεά\[c], τέκνον\[b], and σπέρμα\[b] ([10\.29](#10.29)), the reference is not to one’s immediate descendants or offspring (that is to say, to one’s sons or daughters) but to a successive series of such persons, one’s descendants. In some languages such descendants may be called merely ‘the children of one’s children,’ and in other languages one may refer to descendants as ‘those who follow one’ or ‘those who come later.’

[MAT 1:17](https://ref.ly/Matt1:17) · [MAT 1:17](https://ref.ly/Matt1:17) · [MAT 1:17](https://ref.ly/Matt1:17) · [MAT 1:17](https://ref.ly/Matt1:17) · [LUK 1:48](https://ref.ly/Mark1:48) · [ACT 8:33](https://ref.ly/John8:33)

67\.144 · Time · Indefinite Units of Time: Age, Lifetime, Interval, Period

age, epoch an indefinite period of time, but in close relationship to human existence and in some contexts, a period of time about the length of a generation It is, of course, possible in [ACT 14:16](https://ref.ly/John14:16) that the reference should be to ‘generations’ in the sense of periods of time.

[MAT 24:34](https://ref.ly/Matt24:34) · [LUK 1:50](https://ref.ly/Mark1:50) · [LUK 1:50](https://ref.ly/Mark1:50) · [LUK 21:32](https://ref.ly/Mark21:32) · [ACT 14:16](https://ref.ly/John14:16) · [ACT 15:21](https://ref.ly/John15:21) · [EPH 3:5](https://ref.ly/Gal3:5) · [EPH 3:21](https://ref.ly/Gal3:21) · [COL 1:26](https://ref.ly/Phil1:26)

## γένεσις (id: 001089000000000)

γένεσις
=======

γένεσις (G1078)

noun · γίνομαι

23\.46 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

be born, birth coming into existence by birth A literal translation of [MAT 1:18](https://ref.ly/Matt1:18) as ‘this is the way that Jesus Christ was born’ might be misleading, since it would imply a description of the actual process of his birth rather than an account of those circumstances and events which took place in connection with his birth. It may, therefore, be better to translate [MAT 1:18](https://ref.ly/Matt1:18) as ‘this is what happened when Jesus Christ was born’ or ‘these things happened at the time of Jesus Christ’s birth.’

[MAT 1:18](https://ref.ly/Matt1:18) · [LUK 1:14](https://ref.ly/Mark1:14) · [JAS 1:23](https://ref.ly/Heb1:23)

10\.24 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations Involving Successive Generations

lineage, family line persons of successive generations who are related by birth In biblical times the reckoning of a lineage was somewhat complex in view of certain distinctions between legal and biological relations. The focus of meaning in γένεσις\[b], οἶκος\[c], and πατριά\[a] is not, however, the list of ancestors, but the lineage of successively related persons to which the reference person belongs. Some scholars, however, interpret γένεσις in [MAT 1:1](https://ref.ly/Matt1:1) as being part of what is essentially a title for the book of Matthew and thus would render the introductory phrase as ‘the book of the history of Jesus Christ’ (see γένεσις\[c] ‘history,’ [33\.19](#33.19)).\|In some languages a successive series of ancestors is called ‘the forefathers’ or ‘those to whom one looks back’ or ‘those who have gone ahead.’ In other languages a lineage is referred to as ‘a person’s root’ or ‘a man’s trunk’ (referring to the trunk of a tree).

[MAT 1:1](https://ref.ly/Matt1:1)

33\.19 · Communication · Discourse Types

history an account of the origin and life of someone For the most part, scholars understand the phrase βίβλος γενέσεως in [MAT 1:1](https://ref.ly/Matt1:1) as referring to the list of ancestors which immediately follows. Therefore, βίβλος γενέσεως is more often interpreted as ‘the record of the ancestors’ or ‘the birth record of ...’ (see [10\.24](#10.24)).1

[MAT 1:1](https://ref.ly/Matt1:1)

13\.71 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Exist

existence the state of existence In [JAS 1:23](https://ref.ly/Heb1:23) the term γένεσις is largely redundant, for the reference could only be to a person’s own face.

[JAS 1:23](https://ref.ly/Heb1:23) · [JAS 3:6](https://ref.ly/Heb3:6)

1 See [33\.38](#33.38), where [MAT 1:1](https://ref.ly/Matt1:1) is the illustrative example for βίβλος\[c] ‘written statement,’ ‘record.’ See [23\.46](#23.46) for γένεσις\[a] ‘birth.’

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 1:18; Luke 1:14; James 1:23; Matthew 1:1; James 3:6

7:8](https://ref.ly/John7:8) · [ACT 7:29](https://ref.ly/John7:29) · [ACT 13:33](https://ref.ly/John13:33) · [1CO 4:15](https://ref.ly/Rom4:15) · [PHM 1:10](https://ref.ly/Titus1:10) · [HEB 1:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:5) · [HEB 5:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:5) · [HEB 11:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:12) · [1JN 2:29](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:29) · [1JN 3:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:9) · [1JN 3:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:9) · [1JN 4:7](https://ref.ly/2Pet4:7) · [1JN 5:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:1) · [1JN 5:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:1) · [1JN 5:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:1) · [1JN 5:4](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:4) · [1JN 5:18](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:18)

23\.52 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

to bear, to give birth to give birth to a child1 All languages have expressions for human birth, though these are frequently in idiomatic forms, for example, ‘to drop a child’ or ‘to cause a baby to pass between the legs.’ A number of languages have a variety of terms referring to giving birth, and some of these may involve unfortunate connotations. One must therefore be careful about the selection of appropriate expressions.\|γεννάω also occurs together with ἐξ αἱμάτων ([JHN 1:13](https://ref.ly/Luke1:13)) and ἐκ τῆς σαρκός ([JHN 3:6](https://ref.ly/Luke3:6)) in reference to physical birth. In [JHN 3:5](https://ref.ly/Luke3:5), γεννηθῇ ἐξ ὕδατος has likewise been interpreted by some scholars as referring to physical birth (compare [JHN 3:6](https://ref.ly/Luke3:6)), but others understand this as referring to baptism. Certainly the occurrence of γεννηθῇ with πνεύματος in [JHN 3:5](https://ref.ly/Luke3:5) is a reference to religious rebirth, in which case γεννάω would involve a radical change of state (see [13\.56](#13.56)). The use of the same word with two different meanings or referents is typical of the style of the Gospel of John.

[MAT 1:16](https://ref.ly/Matt1:16) · [MAT 2:1](https://ref.ly/Matt2:1) · [MAT 2:4](https://ref.ly/Matt2:4) · [MAT 19:12](https://ref.ly/Matt19:12) · [MAT 26:24](https://ref.ly/Matt26:24) · [MRK 14:21](https://ref.ly/Matt14:21) · [LUK 1:13](https://ref.ly/Mark1:13) · [LUK 1:35](https://ref.ly/Mark1:35) · [LUK 1:57](https://ref.ly/Mark1:57) · [LUK 23:29](https://ref.ly/Mark23:29) · [JHN 1:13](https://ref.ly/Luke1:13) · [JHN 3:4](https://ref.ly/Luke3:4) · [JHN 3:4](https://ref.ly/Luke3:4) · [JHN 3:5](https://ref.ly/Luke3:5) · [JHN 3:6](https://ref.ly/Luke3:6) · [JHN 9:2](https://ref.ly/Luke9:2) · [JHN 9:19](https://ref.ly/Luke9:19) · [JHN 9:20](https://ref.ly/Luke9:20) · [JHN 9:32](https://ref.ly/Luke9:32) · [JHN 9:34](https://ref.ly/Luke9:34) · [JHN 16:21](https://ref.ly/Luke16:21) · [JHN 16:21](https://ref.ly/Luke16:21) · [JHN 18:37](https://ref.ly/Luke18:37) · [ACT 2:8](https://ref.ly/John2:8) · [ACT 7:20](https://ref.ly/John7:20) · [ACT 22:3](https://ref.ly/John22:3) · [ACT 22:28](https://ref.ly/John22:28) · [ROM 9:11](https://ref.ly/Acts9:11) · [GAL 4:23](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:23) · [GAL 4:29](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:29) · [HEB 11:23](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:23) · [2PE 2:12](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:12)

13\.56 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Change of State

to cause to be born, to be born of (a figurative extension of meaning of γεννάω\[b] ‘to give birth,’ [23\.52](#23.52)) to cause to experience a radical change, with the implication of involvement of the total personality The phrase γεννηθῇ ἐξ ὕδατος has been interpreted by some as a literal reference to physical birth (see [23\.52](#23.52)). Others, however, interpret this phrase as referring to baptism by water. In a parallel fashion, the expression γεννηθῇ ἐξ ... πνεύματος would refer to baptism by the Spirit or rebirth made possible by the Spirit.

[JHN 3:5](https://ref.ly/Luke3:5) · [JHN 3:6](https://ref.ly/Luke3:6) · [JHN 3:8](https://ref.ly/Luke3:8) · [1JN 2:29](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:29) · [1JN 3:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:9) · [1JN 4:7](https://ref.ly/2Pet4:7) · [1JN 5:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:1) · [1JN 5:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:1) · [1JN 5:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:1) · [1JN 5:4](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:4) · [1JN 5:18](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:18) · [1JN 5:18](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:18)

13\.129 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Happen

to cause, to produce, to give rise to to cause to happen, with the implication of the result of existing circumstances

[GAL 4:24](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:24) · [2TI 2:23](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:23)

41\.53 · Behavior and Related States · Change Behavior

**Collocation:** γεννάω ἄνωθεν

to be born again, to experience new birth, rebirth (an idiom, literally: to be born again) to experience a complete change in one’s way of life to what it should be, with the implication of return to a former state or relation It is also possible to understand ἄνωθεν in [JHN 3:3](https://ref.ly/Luke3:3) as meaning ‘from above’ or ‘from God’ (see [84\.13](#84.13)), a literary parallel to the phrase ἐκ θεοῦ ἐγεννήθησαν in [JHN 1:13](https://ref.ly/Luke1:13). In [JHN 3:3](https://ref.ly/Luke3:3), however, Nicodemus understood ἄνωθεν as meaning ‘again’ (see [67\.55](#67.55)) and γεννάω as ‘physical birth’ (see [23\.52](#23.52)).

[JHN 3:3](https://ref.ly/Luke3:3) · [JHN 3:7](https://ref.ly/Luke3:7)

1 It is possible that τεκνογονέω and τεκνογονία differ somewhat in connotation from τίκτω\[a] and γεννάω\[b] in being stylistically more formal, but there seems to be no significant denotative distinction in meaning.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 1:2; Matthew 1:3; Matthew 1:4; Matthew 1:5; Matthew 1:6; Matthew 1:7; Matthew 1:8; Matthew 1:9; Matthew 1:10; Matthew 1:11; Matthew 1:12; Matthew 1:13; Matthew 1:14; Matthew 1:15; Matthew 1:16; Matthew 1:20; Acts 7:8; Acts 7:29; Acts 13:33; 1 Corinthians 4:15; Philemon 1:10; Hebrews 1:5; Hebrews 5:5; Hebrews 11:12; 1 John 2:29; 1 John 3:9; 1 John 4:7; 1 John 5:1; 1 John 5:4; 1 John 5:18; Matthew 2:1; Matthew 2:4; Matthew 19:12; Matthew 26:24; Mark 14:21; Luke 1:13; Luke 1:35; Luke 1:57; Luke 23:29; John 1:13; John 3:4; John 3:5; John 3:6; John 9:2; John 9:19; John 9:20; John 9:32; John 9:34; John 16:21; John 18:37; Acts 2:8; Acts 7:20; Acts 22:3; Acts 22:28; Romans 9:11; Galatians 4:23; Galatians 4:29; Hebrews 11:23; 2 Peter 2:12; John 3:8; Galatians 4:24; 2 Timothy 2:23; John 3:3; John 3:7


## γέννημα (id: 001093000000000)

γέννημα
=======

γέννημα (G1081)

noun · γεννάω

23\.53 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

offspring, brood, child (derivative of γεννάω\[b] ‘to give birth,’ [23\.52](#23.52)) that which has been produced or born of a living creature In some languages it may be possible to translate this phrase in [MAT 3:7](https://ref.ly/Matt3:7) more or less literally, for example, ‘the offspring of vipers,’ in which ‘vipers’ means poisonous snakes, but in other languages this would be impossible, and one must therefore use ‘little snakes.’ For another interpretation of γέννημα in [MAT 3:7](https://ref.ly/Matt3:7), see [58\.26](#58.26).

[MAT 3:7](https://ref.ly/Matt3:7) · [MAT 12:34](https://ref.ly/Matt12:34) · [MAT 23:33](https://ref.ly/Matt23:33) · [LUK 3:7](https://ref.ly/Mark3:7)

58\.26 · Nature, Class, Example · Class, Kind

son of, offspring of, child of, kind of, one who has the characteristics of, person of a kind or class of persons, with the implication of possessing certain derived characteristics For another interpretation of γέννημα in [MAT 3:7](https://ref.ly/Matt3:7), see [23\.53](#23.53).

[MAT 3:7](https://ref.ly/Matt3:7) · [MAT 12:34](https://ref.ly/Matt12:34) · [MAT 23:33](https://ref.ly/Matt23:33) · [LUK 3:7](https://ref.ly/Mark3:7)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 3:7; Matthew 12:34; Matthew 23:33; Luke 3:7

## γεννητός (id: 001095000000000)

γεννητός
========

γεννητός (G1084)

adj · γεννάω

23\.47 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

one born, one who has been born, person (derivative of γεννάω\[b] ‘to give birth,’ [23\.52](#23.52)) pertaining to having been born In some languages a literal rendering of γεννητοῖς γυναικῶν ‘born of women’ could be misleading, for it might suggest that there are persons who have not been born of women. It is for that reason that γεννητοῖς γυναικῶν may be rendered in some instances as ‘of all those persons who have ever lived.’ However, this reference to the preeminence of John the Baptist is difficult, and the implications of it go far beyond the matter of translational equivalence.

[MAT 11:11](https://ref.ly/Matt11:11) · [LUK 7:28](https://ref.ly/Mark7:28)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 11:11; Luke 7:28


## γένος (id: 001096000000000)

γένος
=====

γένος (G1085)

noun · γίνομαι

10\.32 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations Involving Successive Generations

descendant, offspring a non\-immediate descendant (possibly involving a gap of several generations), either male or female In [REV 22:16](https://ref.ly/Jude22:16) ῥίζα\[b] ([10\.33](#10.33)) and γένος\[a] are very similar in meaning, and it is often best to coalesce the two terms into a single expression, for example, ‘I am a descendant of David’ or ‘I belong to the lineage of David.’

[ACT 4:6](https://ref.ly/John4:6) · [ACT 17:28](https://ref.ly/John17:28) · [ACT 17:29](https://ref.ly/John17:29) · [REV 22:16](https://ref.ly/Jude22:16)

10\.1 · Kinship Terms · Groups and Members of Groups of Persons Regarded as Related by Blood but without Special Reference to Successive Generations

race, ethnic group, nation a relatively large group of persons regarded as being biologically related1 It may be difficult in some languages to clearly distinguish between culture and race as in [MRK 7:26](https://ref.ly/Matt7:26). Sometimes this difference can be indicated by saying ‘the woman lived like a Greek, but she was a Syrophoenician’ or ‘... her parents were from Syrophoenicia.’ In translating ‘people of my own race’ in [ROM 11:14](https://ref.ly/Acts11:14), it may be necessary to say ‘all my fellow Jews’ or ‘all those people of whom I am a part’ or ‘those people who are my roots’ or ‘... my trunk,’ based on the analogy of a tree trunk and branches.

[MRK 7:26](https://ref.ly/Matt7:26) · [ACT 4:36](https://ref.ly/John4:36) · [ACT 7:13](https://ref.ly/John7:13) · [ACT 7:19](https://ref.ly/John7:19) · [ACT 13:26](https://ref.ly/John13:26) · [ACT 18:2](https://ref.ly/John18:2) · [ACT 18:24](https://ref.ly/John18:24) · [2CO 11:26](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:26) · [GAL 1:14](https://ref.ly/2Cor1:14) · [PHP 3:5](https://ref.ly/Eph3:5) · [1PE 2:9](https://ref.ly/Jas2:9)

58\.23 · Nature, Class, Example · Class, Kind

kind, type a category or class based upon an implied derivation and/or lineage

[MAT 13:47](https://ref.ly/Matt13:47) · [MRK 9:29](https://ref.ly/Matt9:29) · [ACT 4:6](https://ref.ly/John4:6) · [1CO 12:10](https://ref.ly/Rom12:10) · [1CO 12:28](https://ref.ly/Rom12:28) · [1CO 14:10](https://ref.ly/Rom14:10)

1 πατριά\[a] and φυλή\[b] nation, people ([11\.56](#11.56)) focus attention upon a particular people as a socially functioning unit, while the feature of biological descent is largely secondary. But in the case of γένος\[b] and σάρξ\[e], the feature of biological descent is focal, while group functioning is largely secondary.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 4:6; Acts 17:28; Acts 17:29; Revelation 22:16; Mark 7:26; Acts 4:36; Acts 7:13; Acts 7:19; Acts 13:26; Acts 18:2; Acts 18:24; 2 Corinthians 11:26; Galatians 1:14; Philippians 3:5; 1 Peter 2:9; Matthew 13:47; Mark 9:29; 1 Corinthians 12:10; 1 Corinthians 12:28; 1 Corinthians 14:10

## γερουσία (id: 001099000000000)

γερουσία
========

γερουσία (G1087)

noun · γηράσκω

11\.83 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

Sanhedrin, high council of the Jews the highest council of the Jews (see also συνέδριον\[b] ‘Sanhedrin,’ the council of the Jews, [11\.80](#11.80)) but with the implication of the maturity and relative advanced age of those constituting the membership of such a council1

[ACT 5:21](https://ref.ly/John5:21)

1 Though γερουσία and πρεσβυτέριον\[a] refer to the same council of the Jews as the term συνέδριον\[b] ([11\.80](#11.80)), this does not mean that the three terms are completely identical in meaning. The focus upon maturity of age and judgment as well as presumed social standing are more significant factors in γερουσία and πρεσβυτέριον\[a] than in συνέδριον\[b].

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 5:21

20:8](https://ref.ly/Jude20:8) · [REV 20:9](https://ref.ly/Jude20:9) · [REV 21:1](https://ref.ly/Jude21:1) · [REV 21:1](https://ref.ly/Jude21:1) · [REV 21:24](https://ref.ly/Jude21:24)

1\.60 · Geographical Objects and Features · Land in Contrast With the Sea

land dry land, in contrast with the sea In a number of languages a clear distinction is made between terms which designate land in contrast with water and those which designate cultivated land. Even in English the normal term for land close to water is ‘shore’ or ‘coast,’ and therefore one may translate [MAT 14:24](https://ref.ly/Matt14:24) as ‘the boat was already far away from the shore.’ Similarly, in [ACT 27:27](https://ref.ly/John27:27) one may translate ‘we were getting close to shore.’

[MAT 14:24](https://ref.ly/Matt14:24) · [MAT 14:34](https://ref.ly/Matt14:34) · [MRK 4:1](https://ref.ly/Matt4:1) · [MRK 6:47](https://ref.ly/Matt6:47) · [MRK 6:53](https://ref.ly/Matt6:53) · [LUK 5:3](https://ref.ly/Mark5:3) · [LUK 5:11](https://ref.ly/Mark5:11) · [LUK 8:27](https://ref.ly/Mark8:27) · [JHN 6:21](https://ref.ly/Luke6:21) · [JHN 21:8](https://ref.ly/Luke21:8) · [JHN 21:9](https://ref.ly/Luke21:9) · [JHN 21:11](https://ref.ly/Luke21:11) · [ACT 7:33](https://ref.ly/John7:33) · [ACT 27:43](https://ref.ly/John27:43) · [ACT 27:44](https://ref.ly/John27:44) · [HEB 11:29](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:29) · [JAS 5:17](https://ref.ly/Heb5:17) · [JAS 5:18](https://ref.ly/Heb5:18) · [REV 7:1](https://ref.ly/Jude7:1) · [REV 7:2](https://ref.ly/Jude7:2) · [REV 7:3](https://ref.ly/Jude7:3) · [REV 10:2](https://ref.ly/Jude10:2) · [REV 10:5](https://ref.ly/Jude10:5) · [REV 10:6](https://ref.ly/Jude10:6) · [REV 10:8](https://ref.ly/Jude10:8) · [REV 12:12](https://ref.ly/Jude12:12)

2\.14 · Natural Substances · Earth, Mud, Sand, Rock

soil, ground the loose top layer of earth in which plants grow, usually black, brown, or reddish in color and made of organic matter and mineral particles2 The meaning of γῆ\[c] may be expressed in some instances as soil for planting or ground for plants.

[MAT 13:5](https://ref.ly/Matt13:5) · [MAT 13:5](https://ref.ly/Matt13:5) · [MAT 13:8](https://ref.ly/Matt13:8) · [MAT 13:23](https://ref.ly/Matt13:23) · [MAT 25:18](https://ref.ly/Matt25:18) · [MAT 25:25](https://ref.ly/Matt25:25) · [MRK 4:5](https://ref.ly/Matt4:5) · [MRK 4:5](https://ref.ly/Matt4:5) · [MRK 4:8](https://ref.ly/Matt4:8) · [MRK 4:20](https://ref.ly/Matt4:20) · [MRK 4:26](https://ref.ly/Matt4:26) · [MRK 4:28](https://ref.ly/Matt4:28) · [MRK 4:31](https://ref.ly/Matt4:31) · [LUK 6:49](https://ref.ly/Mark6:49) · [LUK 8:8](https://ref.ly/Mark8:8) · [LUK 8:15](https://ref.ly/Mark8:15) · [LUK 13:7](https://ref.ly/Mark13:7) · [LUK 14:35](https://ref.ly/Mark14:35) · [LUK 22:44](https://ref.ly/Mark22:44) · [LUK 24:5](https://ref.ly/Mark24:5) · [JHN 8:6](https://ref.ly/Luke8:6) · [JHN 8:8](https://ref.ly/Luke8:8) · [JHN 12:24](https://ref.ly/Luke12:24) · [ACT 9:4](https://ref.ly/John9:4) · [ACT 9:8](https://ref.ly/John9:8) · [1CO 15:47](https://ref.ly/Rom15:47) · [HEB 6:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:7) · [JAS 5:7](https://ref.ly/Heb5:7) · [JAS 5:17](https://ref.ly/Heb5:17) · [JAS 5:18](https://ref.ly/Heb5:18) · [REV 14:15](https://ref.ly/Jude14:15) · [REV 14:16](https://ref.ly/Jude14:16) · [REV 14:16](https://ref.ly/Jude14:16) · [REV 14:18](https://ref.ly/Jude14:18) · [REV 14:19](https://ref.ly/Jude14:19) · [REV 14:19](https://ref.ly/Jude14:19) · [REV 16:1](https://ref.ly/Jude16:1) · [REV 16:2](https://ref.ly/Jude16:2)

1\.79 · Geographical Objects and Features · Sociopolitical Areas

region, territory, land (and even district, though this might imply too precisely a governmental area) region or regions of the earth, normally in relation to some ethnic group or geographical center, but not necessarily constituting a unit of governmental administration3 The meanings of γῆ\[d], χώρα\[b], κλίμαὅριον, and μέρος\[c] are not to be regarded as completely synonymous, but in certain of their NT usages they are largely overlapping in reference.

[MAT 2:6](https://ref.ly/Matt2:6) · [MAT 2:20](https://ref.ly/Matt2:20) · [MAT 2:21](https://ref.ly/Matt2:21) · [MAT 4:15](https://ref.ly/Matt4:15) · [MAT 4:15](https://ref.ly/Matt4:15) · [MAT 9:26](https://ref.ly/Matt9:26) · [MAT 9:31](https://ref.ly/Matt9:31) · [MAT 27:45](https://ref.ly/Matt27:45) · [MRK 15:33](https://ref.ly/Matt15:33) · [LUK 23:44](https://ref.ly/Mark23:44) · [JHN 3:22](https://ref.ly/Luke3:22) · [ACT 7:3](https://ref.ly/John7:3) · [ACT 7:3](https://ref.ly/John7:3) · [ACT 7:4](https://ref.ly/John7:4) · [ACT 7:4](https://ref.ly/John7:4) · [ACT 7:6](https://ref.ly/John7:6) · [ACT 7:29](https://ref.ly/John7:29) · [ACT 7:36](https://ref.ly/John7:36) · [ACT 7:40](https://ref.ly/John7:40) · [ACT 13:17](https://ref.ly/John13:17) · [ACT 13:19](https://ref.ly/John13:19) · [ACT 13:19](https://ref.ly/John13:19) · [ACT 27:39](https://ref.ly/John27:39) · [HEB 8:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:9) · [HEB 11:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:9) · [JUD 1:5](https://ref.ly/3John1:5)

9\.22 · People · Human Beings

people, all mankind (figurative extension of meaning of γῆ\[a] ‘earth,’ [1\.39](#1.39)) all people who dwell on the earth

[MAT 5:13](https://ref.ly/Matt5:13) · [MAT 10:15](https://ref.ly/Matt10:15) · [MAT 10:34](https://ref.ly/Matt10:34) · [MAT 11:24](https://ref.ly/Matt11:24) · [MAT 17:25](https://ref.ly/Matt17:25) · [MAT 24:30](https://ref.ly/Matt24:30) · [LUK 12:51](https://ref.ly/Mark12:51) · [LUK 18:8](https://ref.ly/Mark18:8) · [ACT 3:25](https://ref.ly/John3:25) · [ACT 4:26](https://ref.ly/John4:26) · [ROM 9:17](https://ref.ly/Acts9:17) · [ROM 9:28](https://ref.ly/Acts9:28) · [ROM 10:18](https://ref.ly/Acts10:18) · [REV 13:3](https://ref.ly/Jude13:3)

1\.3 · Geographical Objects and Features · Universe, Creation

**Collocation:** ὁ οὐρανὸς καὶ ἡ γῆ

heaven and earth, universe a more or less fixed phrase: the heavens and the earth, equivalent to a single lexical item: the totality of God’s creation There may be certain complications involved in rendering ὁ οὐρανὸς καὶ ἡ γῆ as ‘heaven and earth,’ since ‘heaven’ might be interpreted in some languages as referring only to the dwelling place of God himself. The referents in this passage are ‘the sky and the earth,’ in other words, all of physical existence, but not the dwelling place of God, for the latter would not be included in what is destined to pass away.

[MAT 5:18](https://ref.ly/Matt5:18) · [MAT 11:25](https://ref.ly/Matt11:25) · [MAT 24:35](https://ref.ly/Matt24:35) · [MRK 13:31](https://ref.ly/Matt13:31) · [LUK 10:21](https://ref.ly/Mark10:21) · [LUK 16:17](https://ref.ly/Mark16:17) · [LUK 21:33](https://ref.ly/Mark21:33) · [ACT 4:24](https://ref.ly/John4:24) · [2PE 3:7](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:7) · [REV 14:7](https://ref.ly/Jude14:7) · [REV 20:11](https://ref.ly/Jude20:11)

1 The occurrences of γῆ\[a], οἰκουμένη\[a], and κόσμος\[b] relate specifically to the known inhabited areas of the earth, which in the NT period included the countries bordering on the Mediterranean, the Fertile Crescent as far as the Indus Valley, and as far north in Europe as England and Scandinavia. This was the total known earth or world. Such a restriction to a known area of the earth is also true of terms used in some receptor languages, though the referents are obviously different. What is important is not the particular area of the earth, but the corresponding concept of the surface of the earth as the place of human habitation. It is possible that οἰκουμένη\[a] differs slightly in meaning from γῆ\[a] and κόσμος\[b] in view of a somewhat greater emphasis or focus upon the civilized part of earth. 2 Although in the NT γῆ does not occur as a reference to all solid substances in contrast with fire, air, and water, it does so occur in Classical and Hellenistic Greek. This generic meaning of γῆ as an element is thus not part of the lexical inventory of the NT, but γῆ\[b], a designation for soil, ground, does occur. 3 The overlapping features of meaning in γῆ\[d], χώρα\[b], κλίμα, ὅριον, and μέρος\[c] may be readily illustrated by the comparable overlapping of English terms such as region, territory, and land. For example, in the case of [MAT 15:21](https://ref.ly/Matt15:21) it would be possible to speak of the region of Tyre and Sidon, the territory of Tyre and Sidon, the land of Tyre and Sidon, and even the district of Tyre and Sidon. The English terms region, territory, land, and district do differ in certain nuances of meaning reflecting primarily supplementary components which are largely connotative.

## γῆρας (id: 001107000000000)

γῆρας
=====

γῆρας (G1094)

noun · γηράσκω

67\.157 · Time · Indefinite Units of Time: Age, Lifetime, Interval, Period

old age the period of advanced age, normally of a person beyond his or her prime1

[LUK 1:36](https://ref.ly/Mark1:36)

1 The meanings of terms in [67\.152](#67.152)\-[67\.158](#67.158) could almost be treated equally well in Physiological Processes and States (Domain 23\), since these could be regarded as simply derivatives of physiological states. However, the focus of meaning in the respective contexts seems to be more upon a particular period of time rather than upon a physiological state or condition.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:36


## γηράσκω (id: 001108000000000)

γηράσκω
=======

γηράσκω (G1095)

γέρων · γερουσία · γῆρας

67\.105 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

to grow old, to become old to become old in age (referring to living beings)

[JHN 21:18](https://ref.ly/Luke21:18)1 · [HEB 8:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:13)

1 JHN 21:18 It is also possible to treat γηράσκω in Domain 23 Physiological Processes and States, but the focus in [JHN 21:18](https://ref.ly/Luke21:18) seems to be more upon duration of time than upon a physiological state.

* **Associated Passages:** John 21:18; Hebrews 8:13

13\.48 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Change of State

to become to come to acquire or experience a state In some languages there is no convenient lexical item meaning simply ‘to become,’ but in all instances there are certain paraphrastic expressions which may be employed, for example, ‘to arrive at being’ or ‘to cease being one thing and be another’ or ‘to change to be.’ One must, however, beware in the case of [JHN 1:14](https://ref.ly/Luke1:14) not to employ some expression which would suggest that Christ had lost his divine nature in becoming a person or that he only appeared to be human (docetism).

13\.107 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Happen

to happen, to occur, to come to be to happen, with the implication that what happens is different from a previous state1

21:6](https://ref.ly/Jude21:6) · [REV 22:6](https://ref.ly/Jude22:6)

15\.1 · Linear Movement · Move, Come/Go

to move, to come, to go to make a change of location in space (a highly generic meaning) Though the meaning of γίνομαι is often given as ‘to become,’ it is clear that in contexts such as [ACT 25:15](https://ref.ly/John25:15) and [ACT 27:7](https://ref.ly/John27:7) it would be impossible to render γίνομαι by traditional expressions such as ‘to become.’ In these contexts movement is clearly indicated, and therefore one must frequently employ an expression such as ‘to come to,’ ‘to arrive at,’ or even ‘to travel to.’

[LUK 1:44](https://ref.ly/Mark1:44) · [LUK 3:22](https://ref.ly/Mark3:22) · [LUK 9:35](https://ref.ly/Mark9:35) · [LUK 9:36](https://ref.ly/Mark9:36) · [JHN 6:19](https://ref.ly/Luke6:19) · [JHN 6:21](https://ref.ly/Luke6:21) · [JHN 6:25](https://ref.ly/Luke6:25) · [JHN 10:35](https://ref.ly/Luke10:35) · [ACT 1:18](https://ref.ly/John1:18) · [ACT 13:32](https://ref.ly/John13:32) · [ACT 20:16](https://ref.ly/John20:16) · [ACT 21:17](https://ref.ly/John21:17) · [ACT 25:15](https://ref.ly/John25:15) · [ACT 27:7](https://ref.ly/John27:7) · [GAL 3:14](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:14) · [1TH 1:5](https://ref.ly/Col1:5) · [2TH 2:7](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:7)

30\.77 · Think · To Decide, To Conclude

**Collocation:** γίνομαι γνώμης

to decide, to make up one’s mind (an idiom, literally: to become of a mind) to make up one’s mind, with emphasis upon the process of coming to such a decision5

[ACT 20:3](https://ref.ly/John20:3)

1 This meaning of γίνομαι and ἐπιγίνομαι reflects only a slight shift of focus from the meaning of γίνομαι in [13\.48](#13.48), in which the focus is upon the change. 2 It would also be possible to classify the meaning of γίνομαι\[f] and ὑπάρχω\[d] as belonging to the domain of Relations (89\), especially if one regards the occurrence of the dative of the possessor with γίνομαι\[f] and ὑπάρχω\[d] as being an integral element in the meaning. 3 Of all the meanings in Domain 41 (Behavior and Related States), Subdomain A Behavior, Conduct, γίνομαι\[g] is undoubtedly the most generic and implies the widest possible scope of conduct. 4 ἐγένετο δέ and καὶ ἐγένετο occur frequently in the Gospels, especially in Luke, as markers of transition, and in a number of languages they are equivalent to a new paragraph. Note the following passages especially: [LUK 5:1](https://ref.ly/Mark5:1), [LUK 5:12](https://ref.ly/Mark5:12), [LUK 5:17](https://ref.ly/Mark5:17); [LUK 5:1](https://ref.ly/Mark5:1), [LUK 6:6](https://ref.ly/Mark6:6), [LUK 6:12](https://ref.ly/Mark6:12); [LUK 7:11](https://ref.ly/Mark7:11); [LUK 8:1](https://ref.ly/Mark8:1), [LUK 8:22](https://ref.ly/Mark8:22); [LUK 9:18](https://ref.ly/Mark9:18), [LUK 9:28](https://ref.ly/Mark9:28), [LUK 9:37](https://ref.ly/Mark9:37), [LUK 9:51](https://ref.ly/Mark9:51). 5 γίνομαι γνώμης is similar to τίθημι ἐν τῇ καρδίᾳ and τίθεμαι ἐν τῷ πνεύματι ([30\.76](#30.76)). All relate to the process of decision making, but it is possible that the idioms in [30\.76](#30.76) indicate greater initiative and purpose.

27\.2 · Learn · Learn

to learn, to find out to acquire information by whatever means, but often with the implication of personal involvement or experience

27\.18 · Learn · Learn

to know, to become acquainted with, to be familiar with to learn to know a person through direct personal experience, implying a continuity of relationship In translating γινώσκω in [JHN 17:3](https://ref.ly/Luke17:3), it is important to avoid an expression which will mean merely ‘to learn about.’ Here the emphasis must be on the interpersonal relationship which is experienced.

[JHN 8:55](https://ref.ly/Luke8:55) · [JHN 10:14](https://ref.ly/Luke10:14) · [JHN 10:14](https://ref.ly/Luke10:14) · [JHN 10:15](https://ref.ly/Luke10:15) · [JHN 10:15](https://ref.ly/Luke10:15) · [JHN 10:27](https://ref.ly/Luke10:27) · [JHN 14:7](https://ref.ly/Luke14:7) · [JHN 14:9](https://ref.ly/Luke14:9) · [JHN 14:17](https://ref.ly/Luke14:17) · [JHN 14:17](https://ref.ly/Luke14:17) · [JHN 17:3](https://ref.ly/Luke17:3) · [JHN 17:25](https://ref.ly/Luke17:25) · [JHN 17:25](https://ref.ly/Luke17:25) · [1CO 1:21](https://ref.ly/Rom1:21) · [1CO 8:2](https://ref.ly/Rom8:2) · [GAL 4:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:9) · [EPH 3:19](https://ref.ly/Gal3:19) · [PHP 3:10](https://ref.ly/Eph3:10) · [1JN 2:3](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:3) · [1JN 2:4](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:4) · [1JN 2:13](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:13) · [1JN 2:14](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:14)

32\.16 · Understand · Come To Understand

to come to understand, to perceive, to comprehend to come to an understanding as the result of ability to experience and learn2 It is also possible to interpret γινώσκω in [MAT 13:11](https://ref.ly/Matt13:11) as meaning ‘to know about’ (see [28\.1](#28.1)).

31\.27 · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Acknowledge

to acknowledge to indicate that one does know It is also possible that in [1CO 8:3](https://ref.ly/Rom8:3) γινώσκω means only ‘to know’ ([28\.1](#28.1)).

23\.61 · Physiological Processes and States · Sexual Relations

to have sexual intercourse with (a figurative extension of meaning of γινώσκω\[a] to know, [28\.1](#28.1)) In almost all languages there are euphemistic ways of speaking about sexual intercourse, and the use of γινώσκω\[f] and συνέρχομαι\[c] is illustrative of this in the Greek NT. It is possible to translate γινώσκω in [LUK 1:34](https://ref.ly/Mark1:34) as simply for I am not married to a man, and likewise, συνέρχομαι in [MAT 1:18](https://ref.ly/Matt1:18) may be rendered as ‘before they were married.’ In some languages one may use such expressions as ‘before they were joined’ or ‘before they slept together’ or ‘before they discovered one another.’

[MAT 1:25](https://ref.ly/Matt1:25) · [LUK 1:34](https://ref.ly/Mark1:34)

1 JHN 8:32 In [JHN 8:32](https://ref.ly/Luke8:32) (γνώσεσθε τὴν ἀλήθειανκαὶ ἡ ἀλήθεια ἐλευθερώσει ὑμᾶς ‘you will know the truth and the truth will make you free’), it is also possible to understand γινώσκω as ‘to find out’ or ‘to learn’ ([27\.2](#27.2)). 2 It is possible that ἐπιγινώσκω\[b] differs somewhat in meaning from γινώσκω\[d] in focusing attention on what is understood or indicating that the process of understanding is somewhat more emphatic, but such a distinction cannot be determined from existing contexts.

## γλυκύς (id: 001112000000000)

γλυκύς
======

γλυκύς (G1099)

adj · γλεῦκος

79\.39 · Features of Objects · Sweet, Bitter, Tasteless

sweet, fresh, not bitter, good pertaining to being sweet in contrast with being bitter or salty In a number of languages it would be somewhat misleading to speak of ‘sweet water,’ since this would suggest water to which sugar or some other sweet substance had been added. The equivalent in [JAS 3:11](https://ref.ly/Heb3:11) may be ‘fresh water’ or ‘good water’ in contrast with ‘bad water’ or ‘not bitter water’ in contrast with ‘bitter water.’

[JAS 3:11](https://ref.ly/Heb3:11) · [JAS 3:12](https://ref.ly/Heb3:12) · [REV 10:9](https://ref.ly/Jude10:9) · [REV 10:10](https://ref.ly/Jude10:10)

* **Associated Passages:** James 3:11; James 3:12; Revelation 10:9; Revelation 10:10


## γλῶσσα (id: 001113000000000)

γλῶσσα
======

γλῶσσα (G1100)

noun · γλωσσόκομον · ἑτερόγλωσσος

8\.21 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

tongue organ in the mouth used for speaking and eating Though in [JAS 3:5](https://ref.ly/Heb3:5) the tongue is referred to as a part of the body, it is used essentially as a symbol for speech, and since in some languages the tongue is not regarded as an organ of speech, but simply as a part of the mouth, it may be necessary to change the expression to read ‘the mouth is a small member of the body’ or ‘speaking is only a small part of one’s life.’ It is obviously not the tongue as an organ which corrupts the whole person, but the capacity for speech which has such a corrupting effect.

[MRK 7:33](https://ref.ly/Matt7:33) · [MRK 7:35](https://ref.ly/Matt7:35) · [LUK 16:24](https://ref.ly/Mark16:24) · [ACT 2:3](https://ref.ly/John2:3) · [JAS 3:5](https://ref.ly/Heb3:5) · [JAS 3:6](https://ref.ly/Heb3:6) · [JAS 3:6](https://ref.ly/Heb3:6) · [JAS 3:8](https://ref.ly/Heb3:8) · [REV 16:10](https://ref.ly/Jude16:10)

33\.2 · Communication · Language

language, dialect, speech a language, with the possible implication of its distinctive form The miracle described in [ACT 2:4](https://ref.ly/John2:4) may have been a miracle of speaking or a miracle of hearing, but at any rate people understood fully, and therefore it seems appropriate in this context to speak of ‘languages’ in contrast with [1CO 14:2](https://ref.ly/Rom14:2), in which case people required an interpreter if they were to receive the presumed content of the speech (see [33\.3](#33.3)).

[MRK 16:17](https://ref.ly/Matt16:17) · [ACT 2:4](https://ref.ly/John2:4) · [ACT 2:11](https://ref.ly/John2:11) · [ACT 10:46](https://ref.ly/John10:46) · [ACT 19:6](https://ref.ly/John19:6) · [1CO 12:28](https://ref.ly/Rom12:28) · [1CO 12:30](https://ref.ly/Rom12:30) · [1CO 13:1](https://ref.ly/Rom13:1) · [1CO 14:2](https://ref.ly/Rom14:2) · [1CO 14:4](https://ref.ly/Rom14:4) · [1CO 14:5](https://ref.ly/Rom14:5) · [1CO 14:5](https://ref.ly/Rom14:5) · [1CO 14:6](https://ref.ly/Rom14:6) · [1CO 14:13](https://ref.ly/Rom14:13) · [1CO 14:14](https://ref.ly/Rom14:14) · [1CO 14:18](https://ref.ly/Rom14:18) · [1CO 14:19](https://ref.ly/Rom14:19) · [1CO 14:22](https://ref.ly/Rom14:22) · [1CO 14:23](https://ref.ly/Rom14:23) · [1CO 14:26](https://ref.ly/Rom14:26) · [1CO 14:27](https://ref.ly/Rom14:27) · [1CO 14:39](https://ref.ly/Rom14:39) · [REV 5:9](https://ref.ly/Jude5:9) · [REV 7:9](https://ref.ly/Jude7:9) · [REV 10:11](https://ref.ly/Jude10:11) · [REV 11:9](https://ref.ly/Jude11:9) · [REV 13:7](https://ref.ly/Jude13:7) · [REV 14:6](https://ref.ly/Jude14:6) · [REV 17:15](https://ref.ly/Jude17:15)

33\.3 · Communication · Language

ecstatic language, tongue, ecstatic speech an utterance having the form of language but requiring an inspired interpreter for an understanding of the content Most scholars assume that the phenomena described in [ACT 2:4](https://ref.ly/John2:4) (see [33\.2](#33.2)) and in [1CO 14:2](https://ref.ly/Rom14:2) are significantly different in that in one instance people understood in their own regional language or dialect and in the other instance an interpreter was required. It is for that reason that many interpret γλῶσσα in [1CO 14:2](https://ref.ly/Rom14:2) as ecstatic speech, which was also an element in Hellenistic religions and constituted a symbol of divine inspiration.

[MRK 16:17](https://ref.ly/Matt16:17) · [ACT 10:46](https://ref.ly/John10:46) · [ACT 19:6](https://ref.ly/John19:6) · [1CO 12:10](https://ref.ly/Rom12:10) · [1CO 12:10](https://ref.ly/Rom12:10) · [1CO 12:28](https://ref.ly/Rom12:28) · [1CO 12:30](https://ref.ly/Rom12:30) · [1CO 13:8](https://ref.ly/Rom13:8) · [1CO 14:2](https://ref.ly/Rom14:2)

33\.74 · Communication · Speak, Talk

speech, to speak (figurative extension of meaning of γλῶσσα\[a] ‘tongue,’ [8\.21](#8.21)) to communicate orally

[ACT 2:26](https://ref.ly/John2:26) · [ROM 3:13](https://ref.ly/Acts3:13) · [1CO 14:9](https://ref.ly/Rom14:9) · [JAS 1:26](https://ref.ly/Heb1:26) · [1PE 3:10](https://ref.ly/Jas3:10)

33\.75 · Communication · Speak, Talk

speech, ability to speak (figurative extension of meaning of γλῶσσα\[a] ‘tongue,’ [8\.21](#8.21)) the faculty or capacity for speech In [LUK 1:64](https://ref.ly/Mark1:64) στόμα and γλῶσσα appear to have the same referent and therefore may be regarded as essentially synonymous.

[LUK 1:64](https://ref.ly/Mark1:64)

33\.101 · Communication · Speak, Talk

what is said, talk, utterance that which has been spoken or uttered

[1JN 3:18](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:18)

9\.18 · People · Human Beings

person, individual (a figurative extension of meaning of γλῶσσα\[a] ‘tongue,’ [8\.21](#8.21)) a person as one who utters something1

[ROM 14:11](https://ref.ly/Acts14:11) · [PHP 2:11](https://ref.ly/Eph2:11)

1 In this subdomain (Human Beings) a number of expressions referring to people are based upon metonymies involving terms for parts or aspects of persons. Such metonymic figures of speech are involved in σὰρξ καὶ αἷμα ([9\.14](#9.14)), γόνυ\[b] ([9\.16](#9.16)), χείρ\[b] ([9\.17](#9.17)), γλῶσσα\[g] ([9\.18](#9.18)), ὄνομα\[b] ([9\.19](#9.19)), and ψυχή\[c] ([9\.20](#9.20)).

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 7:33; Mark 7:35; Luke 16:24; Acts 2:3; James 3:5; James 3:6; James 3:8; Revelation 16:10; Mark 16:17; Acts 2:4; Acts 2:11; Acts 10:46; Acts 19:6; 1 Corinthians 12:28; 1 Corinthians 12:30; 1 Corinthians 13:1; 1 Corinthians 14:2; 1 Corinthians 14:4; 1 Corinthians 14:5; 1 Corinthians 14:6; 1 Corinthians 14:13; 1 Corinthians 14:14; 1 Corinthians 14:18; 1 Corinthians 14:19; 1 Corinthians 14:22; 1 Corinthians 14:23; 1 Corinthians 14:26; 1 Corinthians 14:27; 1 Corinthians 14:39; Revelation 5:9; Revelation 7:9; Revelation 10:11; Revelation 11:9; Revelation 13:7; Revelation 14:6; Revelation 17:15; 1 Corinthians 12:10; 1 Corinthians 13:8; Acts 2:26; Romans 3:13; 1 Corinthians 14:9; James 1:26; 1 Peter 3:10; Luke 1:64; 1 John 3:18; Romans 14:11; Philippians 2:11


## γλωσσόκομον (id: 001114000000000)

γλωσσόκομον
===========

γλωσσόκομον (G1101)

noun

6\.143 · Artifacts · Containers

money box a box in which money was kept It may be useful, however, in rendering [JHN 13:29](https://ref.ly/Luke13:29) to say simply ‘Judas had charge of the money’ or ‘Judas was the treasurer of the group,’ since the Greek expression may be understood as an idiom.

[JHN 12:6](https://ref.ly/Luke12:6) · [JHN 13:29](https://ref.ly/Luke13:29)

* **Associated Passages:** John 12:6; John 13:29


## γναφεύς (id: 001115000000000)

γναφεύς
=======

γναφεύς (G1102)

noun · ἄγναφος

48\.7 · Activities Involving Cloth

bleacher, fuller one who cards, cleans, and/or bleaches cloth In [MRK 9:3](https://ref.ly/Matt9:3) the reference is obviously to the process of bleaching, but a γναφεύς also was engaged in the cleaning of cloth as well as carding it, a process by which the nap of cloth was somewhat raised and made soft by being combed with bristles.

[MRK 9:3](https://ref.ly/Matt9:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 9:3

## γνόφος (id: 001118000000000)

γνόφος
======

γνόφος (G1105)

noun

14\.53 · Physical Events and States · Darkness

darkness a condition resulting from the partial or complete absence of light (see [14\.36](#14.36)) In a number of languages it is impossible to speak of ‘darkness’ as being an agent in the sense of [LUK 23:44](https://ref.ly/Mark23:44) ‘darkness covered the whole country.’ Accordingly, one must say ‘throughout the whole country it was dark’ or ‘it darkened over the whole country.’ In some languages darkness may be characterized as being a quality of the night, for example, ‘it was like night.’

[HEB 12:18](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:18)

adj · γινώσκω

[ACT 1:19](https://ref.ly/John1:19) · [ACT 2:14](https://ref.ly/John2:14) · [ACT 4:10](https://ref.ly/John4:10) · [ACT 9:42](https://ref.ly/John9:42) · [ACT 13:38](https://ref.ly/John13:38) · [ACT 15:18](https://ref.ly/John15:18) · [ACT 19:17](https://ref.ly/John19:17) · [ACT 28:22](https://ref.ly/John28:22) · [ACT 28:28](https://ref.ly/John28:28)

28\.30 · Know · Well Known, Clearly Shown, Revealed

[LUK 2:44](https://ref.ly/Mark2:44)

28\.32 · Know · Well Known, Clearly Shown, Revealed

28\.57 · Know · Able To Be Known

what can be known, what is evident, what can be clearly seen pertaining to being able to be known In a number of languages the phrase ‘can be known,’ expressing a capacity relating to a passive state, must be restructured in an active form. This may often be done by rendering [ROM 1:19](https://ref.ly/Acts1:19) as ‘because what people can know about God is clearly evident to these persons’ or ‘they can clearly comprehend what they can know about God’ or ‘because they can clearly see what people can know about God.’

[ROM 1:19](https://ref.ly/Acts1:19)

34\.17 · Association · Associate

friend, acquaintance pertaining to being a friend or acquaintance of someone, and thus enjoying certain privileges as a result of such a relation It is clear that in [JHN 18:15](https://ref.ly/Luke18:15) γνωστός implies much more than simply being ‘well known by.’ To have been simply well known by the High Priest could have been a source of danger for the disciple. It was the fact of a relationship of friendship which made it possible for the disciple to view the proceedings.

[LUK 2:44](https://ref.ly/Mark2:44) · [LUK 23:49](https://ref.ly/Mark23:49) · [JHN 18:15](https://ref.ly/Luke18:15) · [JHN 18:16](https://ref.ly/Luke18:16)

58\.55 · Nature, Class, Example · Unusual, Different From the Ordinary

unusual, extraordinary pertaining to that which is unusual in the sense of being extraordinary For another interpretation of γνωστός in [ACT 4:16](https://ref.ly/John4:16), see γνωστός\[c] [28\.32](#28.32).

[ACT 4:16](https://ref.ly/John4:16)

## γόνυ (id: 001132000000000)

γόνυ
====

γόνυ (G1119)

noun

8\.47 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

knee central hinge joint of the leg where the thigh is joined to the lower leg In [LUK 5:8](https://ref.ly/Mark5:8) the phrase ‘fell on his knees before Jesus’ should normally not be rendered literally since it might imply accidental stumbling. A more satisfactory equivalent may be ‘knelt down before,’ as a sign of worship or gratitude.\|The term γόνυ occurs in a number of idiomatic phrases in the NT. For example, in [HEB 12:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:12) the command ‘to strengthen the weak knees’ should normally not be translated literally, but by an expression meaning ‘to strengthen determination’ or ‘to give courage to’ (see [25\.152](#25.152)). The ‘bending of the knees’ in [MRK 15:19](https://ref.ly/Matt15:19) was a sign of mock respect, and in such a context the term for ‘knee’ is often semantically absorbed into an expression meaning literally ‘bow down before’ (see [53\.61](#53.61)).

[LUK 5:8](https://ref.ly/Mark5:8) · [HEB 12:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:12)

9\.16 · People · Human Beings

person, individual (a figurative extension of meaning of γόνυ\[a] ‘knee,’ [8\.47](#8.47)) a person in the attitude or position of one worshiping or submitting to authority1

[ROM 14:11](https://ref.ly/Acts14:11) · [PHP 2:10](https://ref.ly/Eph2:10)

53\.61 · Religious Activities · Worship, Reverence

**Collocation:** κάμπτω τὸ γόνυ

to worship, to bow before (a Semitic idiom, literally: the knee bends, or: the knee bows) to bend or bow the knee as a symbol of religious devotion2

[ROM 11:4](https://ref.ly/Acts11:4) · [ROM 14:11](https://ref.ly/Acts14:11) · [EPH 3:14](https://ref.ly/Gal3:14)

25\.152 · Attitudes and Emotions · Encouragement, Consolation

**Collocation:** τὰ παραλελυμένα γόνατα ἀνορθόω

to become encouraged, to encourage oneself by determination (an idiom, literally: straighten paralyzed knees) to gain encouragement by a strong resolve See discussion at [23\.170](#23.170).

[HEB 12:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:12)

17\.19 · Stances and Events Related to Stances · Kneel

**Collocation:** τίθημι τὰ γόνατα

to kneel down, to kneel (an idiom, literally: to place the knees, a Latinism) to kneel down before, with the implication of an act of reverence or of supplication In a number of cultures, kneeling does not imply either reverence or an act of supplication. In some instances translators have used a functional substitute involving a similar type of stance, namely, ‘to bow low before,’ but it may be necessary to use a more or less literal description of ‘kneeling before’ and then to place in a marginal note an indication of the implications of such an act.

[MRK 15:19](https://ref.ly/Matt15:19) · [LUK 22:41](https://ref.ly/Mark22:41) · [ACT 7:60](https://ref.ly/John7:60) · [ACT 9:40](https://ref.ly/John9:40) · [ACT 20:36](https://ref.ly/John20:36) · [ACT 21:5](https://ref.ly/John21:5)

1 In this subdomain (Human Beings) a number of expressions referring to people are based upon metonymies involving terms for parts or aspects of persons. Such metonymic figures of speech are involved in σὰρξ καὶ αἷμα ([9\.14](#9.14)), γόνυ\[b] ([9\.16](#9.16)), χείρ\[b] ([9\.17](#9.17)), γλῶσσα\[g] ([9\.18](#9.18)), ὄνομα\[b] ([9\.19](#9.19)), and ψυχή\[c] ([9\.20](#9.20)). 2 One may also interpret the idiom κάμπτω τὸ γόνυ as consisting of a metonymy in the case of τὸ γόνυ (in other words, knee as a substitute for person). Accordingly, κάμπτω to bend or to bow could then be interpreted as meaning simply to worship.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 5:8; Hebrews 12:12; Romans 14:11; Philippians 2:10; Romans 11:4; Ephesians 3:14; Mark 15:19; Luke 22:41; Acts 7:60; Acts 9:40; Acts 20:36; Acts 21:5

γονυπετέω
=========

γονυπετέω (G1120)

17\.19 · Stances and Events Related to Stances · Kneel

to kneel down, to kneel to kneel down before, with the implication of an act of reverence or of supplication In a number of cultures, kneeling does not imply either reverence or an act of supplication. In some instances translators have used a functional substitute involving a similar type of stance, namely, ‘to bow low before,’ but it may be necessary to use a more or less literal description of ‘kneeling before’ and then to place in a marginal note an indication of the implications of such an act.

[MAT 17:14](https://ref.ly/Matt17:14) · [MAT 27:29](https://ref.ly/Matt27:29) · [MRK 1:40](https://ref.ly/Matt1:40) · [MRK 10:17](https://ref.ly/Matt10:17)

## γράμμα (id: 001134000000000)

γράμμα
======

γράμμα (G1121) — γράμματα

noun · γράφω

33\.35 · Communication · Written Language

letter a letter of the Greek alphabet1

[2CO 3:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:7) · [GAL 6:11](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:11)

33\.50 · Communication · Written Language

writing, what has been written any kind of written document, whether in book or manuscript form, with focus upon the content

[JHN 5:47](https://ref.ly/Luke5:47) · [ACT 28:21](https://ref.ly/John28:21) · [ROM 2:27](https://ref.ly/Acts2:27) · [ROM 2:29](https://ref.ly/Acts2:29) · [ROM 7:6](https://ref.ly/Acts7:6) · [2CO 3:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:6) · [2CO 3:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:6) · [2TI 3:15](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:15)

6\.63 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Marking and Writing

letter an object containing writing addressed to one or more persons, normally written on papyrus2 In some languages it may be necessary to try to distinguish between a letter as an object and a letter as content or message. In [ACT 23:33](https://ref.ly/John23:33) the focus seems to be upon the letter as an object, not necessarily upon the contents of the document. In most contexts, however, it is impossible to distinguish between a letter as a material object and a letter as a message (see [33\.48](#33.48)).

[ACT 28:21](https://ref.ly/John28:21)

33\.39 · Communication · Written Language

account, record of debts a written statement of financial accounts, especially of debts In place of the expression ‘here is your account,’ one may say ‘here is a list of what you owe.’

[LUK 16:6](https://ref.ly/Mark16:6) · [LUK 16:7](https://ref.ly/Mark16:7)

27\.21 · Learn · Learn

learning, education, scholarship (pl; των n) the body of information acquired in school or from the study of writings For a discussion of problems involved in translating [JHN 7:15](https://ref.ly/Luke7:15), see μανθάνω\[a] ([27\.12](#27.12)).

[JHN 7:15](https://ref.ly/Luke7:15) · [ACT 26:24](https://ref.ly/John26:24)

1 α, β, and γ, the first three letters of the Greek alphabet, are used as ordinal numbers (first, second, and third) in connection with the titles of books of the NT. See Domain 60 Number. 2 γράμμα\[c] may also be classified as a derivative of γράφω to write ([33\.61](#33.61)) and mean anything that is written; see [33\.50](#33.50).

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 3:7; Galatians 6:11; John 5:47; Acts 28:21; Romans 2:27; Romans 2:29; Romans 7:6; 2 Corinthians 3:6; 2 Timothy 3:15; Luke 16:6; Luke 16:7; John 7:15; Acts 26:24

27\.22 · Learn · Learn

scholar, teacher a person who has acquired a high level of education in a certain body of literature or discipline In traditional translations γραμματεύς in contexts such as [1CO 1:20](https://ref.ly/Rom1:20) and [MAT 13:52](https://ref.ly/Matt13:52) has been rendered as ‘scribe,’ but this generally is misleading since the term ‘scribe’ is usually restricted in meaning to one who writes or copies documents. A γραμματεύς in Jewish life of Bible times would have been an expert in the Law or a scholar in the Holy Scriptures and not a mere copier of manuscripts.

[MAT 13:52](https://ref.ly/Matt13:52) · [MAT 23:34](https://ref.ly/Matt23:34) · [1CO 1:20](https://ref.ly/Rom1:20)

37\.94 · Control, Rule · Rule, Govern

[ACT 19:35](https://ref.ly/John19:35)

## γραφή (id: 001137000000000)

γραφή
=====

γραφή (G1124) — γραφαί

noun · γράφω

33\.10 · Communication · Word, Passage

passage, part of a document, part of Scripture a particular portion or unit of discourse1 In rendering τόπος\[b], περιοχή, or γραφή\[a], it is often possible to use a rather general term such as the place or the part. In other instances one may wish to use a term meaning the words. Accordingly, [LUK 4:21](https://ref.ly/Mark4:21) may be rendered as ‘these words have come true today as you have heard them being read.’

[LUK 4:21](https://ref.ly/Mark4:21)

33\.53 · Communication · Written Language

Scripture, Scripture passage a particular passage of the OT2

[MRK 12:10](https://ref.ly/Matt12:10) · [LUK 4:21](https://ref.ly/Mark4:21) · [JHN 2:22](https://ref.ly/Luke2:22) · [JHN 7:38](https://ref.ly/Luke7:38) · [JHN 7:42](https://ref.ly/Luke7:42) · [JHN 10:35](https://ref.ly/Luke10:35) · [JHN 13:18](https://ref.ly/Luke13:18) · [JHN 17:12](https://ref.ly/Luke17:12) · [JHN 19:24](https://ref.ly/Luke19:24) · [JHN 19:28](https://ref.ly/Luke19:28) · [JHN 19:36](https://ref.ly/Luke19:36) · [JHN 19:37](https://ref.ly/Luke19:37) · [JHN 20:9](https://ref.ly/Luke20:9) · [ACT 1:16](https://ref.ly/John1:16) · [ACT 8:32](https://ref.ly/John8:32) · [ACT 8:35](https://ref.ly/John8:35) · [ROM 4:3](https://ref.ly/Acts4:3) · [ROM 9:17](https://ref.ly/Acts9:17) · [ROM 10:11](https://ref.ly/Acts10:11) · [ROM 11:2](https://ref.ly/Acts11:2) · [GAL 3:8](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:8) · [GAL 3:22](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:22) · [GAL 4:30](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:30) · [1TI 5:18](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:18) · [2TI 3:16](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:16) · [JAS 2:8](https://ref.ly/Heb2:8) · [JAS 2:23](https://ref.ly/Heb2:23) · [JAS 4:5](https://ref.ly/Heb4:5) · [1PE 2:6](https://ref.ly/Jas2:6) · [2PE 1:20](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:20)

33\.54 · Communication · Written Language

the Scriptures, the holy writings (pl; ῶν f) the sacred writings of the OT Some translators have mistakenly attempted to use the rendering ‘Bible’ when translating αἱ γραφαί ‘the Scriptures’ in the NT. The reference is to the OT and not to the entire Bible, including both New and Old Testaments. It is also a mistake to translate αἱ γραφαί as ‘God’s writings,’ for this would give the impression that God himself wrote the words.

[MAT 21:42](https://ref.ly/Matt21:42) · [MAT 22:29](https://ref.ly/Matt22:29) · [MAT 26:54](https://ref.ly/Matt26:54) · [MAT 26:56](https://ref.ly/Matt26:56) · [MRK 12:24](https://ref.ly/Matt12:24) · [MRK 14:49](https://ref.ly/Matt14:49) · [LUK 24:27](https://ref.ly/Mark24:27) · [LUK 24:32](https://ref.ly/Mark24:32) · [LUK 24:45](https://ref.ly/Mark24:45) · [JHN 5:39](https://ref.ly/Luke5:39) · [ACT 17:2](https://ref.ly/John17:2) · [ACT 17:11](https://ref.ly/John17:11) · [ACT 18:24](https://ref.ly/John18:24) · [ACT 18:28](https://ref.ly/John18:28) · [ROM 1:2](https://ref.ly/Acts1:2) · [ROM 15:4](https://ref.ly/Acts15:4) · [1CO 15:3](https://ref.ly/Rom15:3) · [1CO 15:4](https://ref.ly/Rom15:4) · [2PE 3:16](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:16)

1 γραφή\[a] in [33\.10](#33.10) differs significantly in meaning from γραφή\[b] ([33\.53](#33.53)) in that the latter denotes specifically some OT Scripture passage, while γραφή\[a] is a more generic reference to any unit of discourse, though in [LUK 4:21](https://ref.ly/Mark4:21) it happens to refer to an OT section. 2 For γραφή in the more generic sense, see [33\.10](#33.10) and footnote.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 4:21; Mark 12:10; John 2:22; John 7:38; John 7:42; John 10:35; John 13:18; John 17:12; John 19:24; John 19:28; John 19:36; John 19:37; John 20:9; Acts 1:16; Acts 8:32; Acts 8:35; Romans 4:3; Romans 9:17; Romans 10:11; Romans 11:2; Galatians 3:8; Galatians 3:22; Galatians 4:30; 1 Timothy 5:18; 2 Timothy 3:16; James 2:8; James 2:23; James 4:5; 1 Peter 2:6; 2 Peter 1:20; Matthew 21:42; Matthew 22:29; Matthew 26:54; Matthew 26:56; Mark 12:24; Mark 14:49; Luke 24:27; Luke 24:32; Luke 24:45; John 5:39; Acts 17:2; Acts 17:11; Acts 18:24; Acts 18:28; Romans 1:2; Romans 15:4; 1 Corinthians 15:3; 1 Corinthians 15:4; 2 Peter 3:16


## γράφω (id: 001138000000000)

γράφω
=====

γράφω (G1125) — γέγραπται

ἀγράμματος · ἀπογραφή · ἀπογράφω · γράμμα · γραμματεύς · γραπτός · γραφή · ἐγγράφω · ἐπιγραφή · ἐπιγράφω · καταγράφω · προγράφω · ὑπογραμμός · χειρόγραφον

33\.61 · Communication · Written Language

to write to make the marks that form words on a surface (paper or other material), using a marking instrument (such as a pen) Since the knowledge of writing is almost universal, there is usually no difficulty in obtaining a satisfactory term for writing. In some instances in which languages are only now being reduced to writing, a phrase is often employed, for example, ‘to make marks on paper’ or ‘to talk with lines’ or ‘to speak with paper.’

23\.72 · Physiological Processes and States · Sleep, Waking

## γυμνάζω (id: 001142000000000)

γυμνάζω
=======

γυμνάζω (G1128)

γυμνασία · γυμνιτεύω · γυμνός · γυμνότης

88\.88 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Self\-Control, Lack of Self\-Control

to discipline oneself, to keep oneself disciplined to control oneself by thorough discipline In a number of languages the equivalent of ‘to discipline oneself’ is literally ‘to make oneself obey.’ This may sometimes be expressed idiomatically as ‘to command one’s heart.’

[1TI 4:7](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:7)

36\.11 · Guide, Discipline, Follow · Discipline, Train

to train, to undergo discipline to experience vigorous training and control, with the implication of increased physical and/or moral strength In rendering γυμνάζω in [HEB 12:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:11) it may be important in some languages to translate ‘those who have learned by such punishment’ or ‘those whose ways have been made right by such punishment’ or ‘those who because of punishment have learned how they must act.’

[HEB 5:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:14) · [HEB 12:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:11) · [2PE 2:14](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:14)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Timothy 4:7; Hebrews 5:14; Hebrews 12:11; 2 Peter 2:14

[MAT 25:36](https://ref.ly/Matt25:36) · [MAT 25:38](https://ref.ly/Matt25:38) · [MAT 25:43](https://ref.ly/Matt25:43) · [MAT 25:44](https://ref.ly/Matt25:44) · [MRK 14:51](https://ref.ly/Matt14:51) · [MRK 14:52](https://ref.ly/Matt14:52) · [JHN 21:7](https://ref.ly/Luke21:7) · [ACT 19:16](https://ref.ly/John19:16) · [1CO 15:37](https://ref.ly/Rom15:37) · [2CO 5:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:3) · [JAS 2:15](https://ref.ly/Heb2:15) · [REV 3:17](https://ref.ly/Jude3:17) · [REV 16:15](https://ref.ly/Jude16:15) · [REV 17:16](https://ref.ly/Jude17:16)

28\.62 · Know · Able To Be Known

not hidden, easily known, naked (a figurative extension of meaning of γυμνός\[a] ‘naked,’ [49\.22](#49.22)) easily able to be known in view of the fact that nothing is hidden It is rare that one can employ in translating γυμνός b a term which literally means ‘naked,’ but it is possible to retain something of the metaphorical value by using a phrase such as ‘with nothing to cover’ or ‘with nothing which can be used to hide.’

[HEB 4:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:13)

## γυνή (id: 001149000000000)

γυνή
====

γυνή (G1135)

noun · γυναικάριον · γυναικεῖος

9\.34 · People · Females

woman an adult female person of marriageable age In some languages it may be awkward to speak of ‘arresting men and women,’ since it is normal in such languages to speak of ‘men and women’ simply as ‘people.’ However, where the distinction of ‘men and women’ can be employed, it should be done, since the arresting of women for presumed heresy in NT times would seem far less justified than the arresting of men, who were supposed to take a more active part in new movements and thus were more likely to be arraigned before authorities.\|As a form of address, γυνή was used in Koine Greek in speaking politely to a female person: ὦ γύναι, μεγάλη σου ἡ πίστις ‘Lady, your faith is great’ [MAT 15:28](https://ref.ly/Matt15:28). In [JHN 2:4](https://ref.ly/Luke2:4) Jesus uses γυνή to address his mother courteously.\|In a number of languages it would be totally impossible to have Jesus address his mother merely as ‘woman.’ To do so in some languages would imply that Jesus was denying that Mary was his mother. In other languages, such an expression would imply that Jesus was calling his mother a prostitute or evil person. Accordingly, in a number of languages there is simply no other way in which Jesus could address his mother than as ‘mother’ or ‘my mother.’

10\.54 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations Based upon Marriage

wife a woman who is married to a man The distinctions in meaning of γυνή\[a] woman ([9\.34](#9.34)) and γυνή\[b] wife parallel those involving ἀνήρ\[c] and ἄνθρωπος\[c] (see [10\.53](#10.53)). A number of languages, however, employ essentially the same usage as Greek in that a wife is simply called his woman, my woman, etc. The contexts normally indicate clearly which meaning of γυνή is involved.

34\.70 · Association · Marriage, Divorce

**Collocation:** γυναικὸς ἅπτομαι

to marry, to get married (an idiom, literally: to touch a woman) to marry a woman It is important to note that this expression in the second part of [1CO 7:1](https://ref.ly/Rom7:1) may be either a statement by Paul or a quotation from a letter from the church of Corinth. This fact should be clearly noted in the margin.

[1CO 7:1](https://ref.ly/Rom7:1)

**Collocation:** λαμβάνω γυναῖκα

to marry, to get married (an idiom, literally: to take a woman) to marry a woman
